Now, twenty-five years later, the quantum entanglement that bound these musicians has reached critical mass, creating a temporal anomaly that threatens to collapse the space-time continuum unless they reconvene and complete the sonic ritual they began at a Nashville high school decades ago. Jay Sanders-last seen communicating with entities from the music of the spheres-has been pulled from his Tuesday night quantum residency. Jason Krekel materialized mid-letterpress print, his guitar still vibrating at frequencies that transcend the four-track cassette dimension. What began as a student club has evolved into a living organism, a sentient musical algorithm that spans decades and continents, pulling its scattered members back together like cosmic debris orbiting an invisible singularity. This isn't nostalgia. This is the universe demanding completion of an unfinished equation written in sound waves and string theory. Witness the AVAS Continuum. Watch out for aliens. Bring your third eye. Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Unknown
Host: Little Jumbo Bar
Tags: Live Music, Nightlife
Description: Sanders, Boyd, Page & Hall distill the pure essence of improvisational expression, converging as alchemists of sound, transmuting musical elements into their most essential forms. This quartet embodies the philosophical concept of quintessence-the fifth element beyond earth, air, fire, and water-representing the fundamental substance from which all musical reality springs. Their original compositions crystallize the essential qualities of diverse influences, oscillating between through-composed musical themes, groove-based soul explorations, traditional jazz-influenced pieces, Americana-inspired peaceful melodicism, world music influences, free jazz adventures, and occasional forays into cacophonous noise music. Through years of improvisational study, they've learned to access that rarefied space where genres dissolve into pure creative energy. In this musical laboratory, Sanders' guitar becomes a conduit for universal vibration, Boyd's reeds channel the breath of consciousness itself, Page's bass provides the fundamental frequency of existence, while Hall's percussion creates the rhythmic heartbeat of the cosmos.

Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: AmeriHealth Caritas
Tags: Networking, Education, Community
Description: Join us at AmeriHealth Caritas Wellness Center for an **Introduction to AI Basics for Beginners** Workshop.

**WHEN: Tuesday, December 2nd, 9:30AM-11AM**

**WHERE: 216 Asheland Avenue, PARK LOWER PARKING LOT (South facing) and enter front doors - AmeriHealth Caritas Wellness & Opportunity Center**

This seminar is hosted by **Rylan Lovejoy** (owner of Lovejoy Innovative Planning) and **Jacob Underwood** (owner of Modern Merchant Solutions). Both Rylan and Jacob are **Asheville natives** who have joined forces after seeing the rapid expansion of AI integration in the local community. They sit on the same BNI chapter and are committed to creating a learning atmosphere to help small businesses and solo-preneurs **adapt and thrive** with technology. This seminar‚Äîthe first of their collaboration‚Äîwill dive into the **benefits and risks** associated with AI integration, promoting growth not just for individual businesses, but for the local economy as a whole because when local small business thrives the whole community does too.

This event will be an introduction to best practices, pitfalls to watch out for, and a free packet of ready-to-use prompts & instructions you can put to use. The path to learning how to adapt and integrate AI into your professional life.

What You'll Gain:

Understanding of core AI integration best practices

Knowledge of common professional pitfalls to avoid

A free, ready-to-use prompt packet for immediate application

**Words from your host:**

*Rylan Lovejoy:* "I decided to launch my own business when I realized that the more people I talk to and the more rapid information spreads. I have found that folks do not lack the ability to find answers, but need to know the right questions to ask. With that, some of the most fundamental headaches I have found business owners deal with is sourcing the right question for their unique situation. It cost one of two things: your time or your money. I have found that some of the money charged to find those questions is, in my opinion, ridiculous. So with that, my business was born. Everything we do is from a how to help educate standpoint. Not just financially, but with tech, ai, sales, taxes, and much more. I have built this firm that is rooted in community, delivering clarity, built on transparency. No more are the days where information is what keeps innovation at bay."

Nia Dance Fitness
When: Tue, Dec 2, 10:30 AM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: $15
Host: Dragon Phoenix
Tags: Dance, Fitness, Wellness
Description: An empowering Dance Fitness class that you will love coming back to week after week.

Nia is a sensory-based movement practice that draws from martial arts, dance arts and healing arts. It empowers people of all shapes and sizes by connecting the body, mind, emotions and spirit. Classes are taken barefoot to soul-stirring music in more than 45 countries.

Nia draws from Tai Chi, Tae Kwon Do, Aikido, jazz dance, modern dance, Duncan dance, yoga, Alexander Technique and Teachings of Moshe Feldenkrais. Every class offers a unique combination of 52 moves that correspond with the main areas of the body: the base, the core and the upper extremities

Through a fusion of martial arts, dance arts, and healing arts, Nia brings the body, mind, emotions, and spirit to optimal health through music, movement, and self expression. ¬†Nia connects us to the wisdom of the body through the sensations of comfort, pleasure, and ease. ¬†Each class is a blend of fun choreography, freedance, Floorplay, and your own personal movement creativity. ¬†Non-intimidating, effective, kind to bones and joints, dynamic movement, sweaty fun!

Gentle Flow: These classes are suitable for beginners as well as experienced students. Gentle Flow will offer some flow, including some movements up and down off of the mat. Postures may include, but are not limited to, sitting, hands & knees, standing poses, balancing poses, etc. Expect lots of modifications and cues to help you have the safest practice possible.

Suitable for Beginners: Anything with ‚ÄúGentle‚Äù in the title. Students of all levels will find these classes accessible. Although more challenging poses and sequences may be offered at times, modifications will be given to make the practice accessible to everyone.

Holiday Pub Club: Ugly Sweater Contest
When: Tue, Dec 2, 5:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: Asheville Young Professionals (AYPROS)
Tags: Networking, Nightlife, Holiday, Markets
Description: We‚Äôre closing out the year with one of our favorite AYPROS traditions: the December Pub Club at Pillar Rooftop Bar! The space transforms into its annual holiday pop-up, complete with winter d√©cor, a festive atmosphere, and some of the best views in downtown Asheville. It‚Äôs a relaxed, easy (and free!) way to connect with other young professionals as we wrap up 2025.
Whether you‚Äôve been diving into AYPROS programs all year or you‚Äôre just getting plugged in, this is a great final meetup before the holidays slow everything down.

Scenic AVL #9 - Downtown to Windswept from First Baptist Church
When: Tue, Dec 2, 5:45 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: The Asheville Hiking Group
Tags: Outdoors, Tours, Holiday, Fitness, Nightlife
Description: **Meeting Place:** Park in the First Baptist Church parking lot between the church and the YMCA.
**Gear:** Please bring a flashlight OR headlamp. We will walk through some woods, and it will be dark!!
**Meeting Point:** [https://maps.app.goo.gl/zYYZFLSk7rg4pdrP6](https://maps.app.goo.gl/zYYZFLSk7rg4pdrP6)
**Rating:** Strenuous for Pace and Distance
**Surface:** Road and some trail
**Mileage:** about 5.5 miles
**Elevation Gain:** 750
**Pace:** 3.0 mph flats, slower on steep climbs. We will stop at the top of Windswept for a short break, and we will finish within 2 hours. We walk at a pretty fast pace, so please be aware of your capabilities.
**Features:** Downtown points of interest, views from Windswept. The Christmas decorations should be out!
**After Eats:** Taco Temple
Bears not likely, but we did see one a couple months ago.

**Scenic Asheville Series:** There are 10 hikes in the [series](https://docs.google.com/document/d/11ewlUM9OV8I4npc1cNNsSYOnXI0QPw2isAleXdFzEbI/edit?usp=drivesdk); hike 9 of them and receive an attractive [badge](https://docs.google.com/drawings/d/1goXUXfzUBqhB4_UeCxodlk4ZPeCCgqZrWK2EUJvk_vI/edit) for your backpack. Check your progress [HERE](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1XUm-X1_OhxKIi8JU5rhjsW37cAl4yYx8yB_NEjjI5Lk/edit?usp=sharing).

**General Route:** [Avl Urban Trail to Windswept](https://www.alltrails.com/explore/map/evening-hike-at-avl-urban-trail-to-windswept-7949e45)
Here is the full list of waypoints, but the route will be adjusted for winter so we will not stop for all of them: [Downtown to Windswept Waypoints](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1h6VbzxQjBE8Ha6X8kfX9Hhtvn9LE-Q5BgD_Uz12SE-c/edit?usp=sharing)

RSVP and On-Time Start:

* If you decide you cannot come, please change your RSVP
* If you must cancel, please change your status to "Not Going" as soon as possible so wait-listers can have sufficient notice.
* There are generally 1 or 2 no-shows on my hikes, so we don't wait for people to arrive. If you are late, you'll be left behind.
* Notes and comments are genuinely appreciated.

**NO Guests**: Please ask guests to sign up for the hike themselves.

**Disclaimer and Release of Liability:**
This activity involves hiking on city streets that may have traffic. Participants are responsible for their safety on streets and trails. The organizer of this trip is a volunteer and not a professional guide. The function of the organizer is only to organize this trip. Shut Up & Write!¬Æ - Downtown
When: Tue, Dec 2, 6:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: Shut Up & Write!¬Æ Western North Carolina
Tags: Networking, Education, Community, Book Club
Description: Shut Up & Write!

**Here's how it works.** Show up at or before 6:00. At 6:00, we do some quick introductions. Afterward, for a full 60 minutes (I'll set a timer!) we are heads-down writing. Writing what? A novel? You bet. Some poetry? Sure. Song lyrics? Your resume? That report you need to get to your boss before 8 AM or you'll *need* *to write* that resume? All of the above and more. Just shut up and write.

Surrounding ourselves with other writers who are busy putting words onto page (physical or virtual) keeps us all accountable and focused.

When the timer goes off, we'll check-in with each other and see how it went. Afterward, feel free to stay to chat and get to know your fellow writers, or keep writing, or take off.

Socializing is optional and will happen after (or briefly before) the focused writing. This is a safe space to work on your craft. No one will read or critique your writing.

For more information about our events, visit [https://shutupwrite.com](https://shutupwrite.com).

**What to Expect**

* Roughly 15 minutes of introductions
* 60 minutes of focused writing (somebody set a timer)!
* Afterward, optional socializing

**Being late is okay:** Just show up and get settled, then check in with the host after the session. (Look for the person with the Shut Up & Write sign).

**What Should I Bring?**

* Whatever you need to be able to write!
* Earbuds/earplugs if you want to block ambient noise.

**Other Important Details:**

HOSTS: This is a multi-host event, so most of the time there will be a host present. If we are unlucky and no host can attend, please find each other and self-organize. Pay attention to the event chat and comments to see who is available.

WI-FI: Yes!

PARKING: Street parking in metered spots is free after 6pm. Closest municipal garages ($2/hour) are Wall St. & Coxe Street/Sears Alley.

**This will be a 4 part series for platonic touch with the same group of people all 4 weeks. By making this a series, we will not spend much time reviewing consent each time. Time: this series is from 7-9:30pm. You may show up at 6:50 to make sure you are here at the beginning.
**This is a non-sexual touch based event that invites participants to explore platonic intimacy in a safe environment** with like-minded people. We respect personal boundaries and through a supportive framework of mutual agreements that maximize safety and create a space of easy openness and compassionate connection.

1\. Clothes stay on for the whole event\.
2\. You do not have to touch anyone at this event\.
3\. You must receive a verbal YES before you touch anyone\.
4\. Take care of yourself and those you choose to interact with\.
5\. Speak up if you have a question\, concern\, or if you need assistance with anything during the event\.
6\. All emotions are welcome\- we love vulnerability\.
**WHY CUDDLE?**
Touch is a basic human need, and many of us do not get enough; most people don‚Äôt even know they are missing touch, or have a way to ask for touch without sexualizing it. We believe deeply in the power of touch, and the importance of communication and consent in creating a safe space for touch.
CUDDLING WITH STRANGERS
Cuddling with strangers sounds weird or scary to most people. ‚ÄúWill I like it?‚Äù ‚ÄúWhat if someone wants to touch me and I don‚Äôt want to?‚Äù ‚ÄúWhat if I say yes and it‚Äôs not what I want?‚Äù ‚ÄúWhat if I really want to touch someone and they say no?‚Äù These are all normal questions. The answer is that this is a space created to ask for exactly what you want, and receive NOTHING you don‚Äôt want. Many people start out nervous at a cuddle event & most are really glad they came.

**ETIQUETTE**

* ARRIVE ON TIME: It is important that all participants arrive before the Welcome Circle. The Welcome Circle serves the purpose of creating the safe space for consensual, non-sexual touch between participants and making sure that everyone is informed about consent.
* Please arrive clean & as scent free as possible.
* BE SOBER: Please do not drink or smoke before or at this event.

**WHAT TO BRING:** personal water bottle and snacks to share, a friend, a date ‚Äì whatever cuddle accessories you like! The only thing that you are required to bring is a clean and sober you.

These events are not "gender balanced".

**We take individual and group safety seriously!** If you experience, see, or know that one of our participants is not safe to be at this event we want to know about it. We are committed to doing our best to create a safe environment which means that if someone is causing harm (physical or mental) that person is not welcome here (this includes harm that takes place outside of our events). We stand behind survivors and know that some of our participants are here to heal from touch based trauma.

\*refund policy-
Full refund if you cancel 7 days before the event or you cancel due to illness, emergency, or direct exposure to covid/flu.
Credit towards a future event if you cancel more than 3 days before an event.
No refund if you cancel within 2 days of the event or no-show.

Hannah Juanita w/ Resonant Rogues
When: Tue, Dec 2, 8:00 PM
Where: The Grey Eagle
Price: $18.45
Host: The Grey Eagle
Tags: Live Music, Family
Description: ALL AGESSTANDING ROOM ONLY HANNAH JUANITA Hannah Juanita left her home state of Tennessee in her early twenties, excited to meet the world. She travelled in search of herself, worked odd jobs, and spent countless nights singing fireside under the stars with friends, never pursuing music as a career. Eventually, Hannah made it back to Tennessee, landing in Nashville with nothing but her dog Loretta, her guitar, and a handful of heartbreak songs. She started singing around town and quickly became a staple live performer and a highly respected vocalist in the traditional country scene in Music City, known for her classic, old school sound. Self proclaimed ramblin' gal, Hannah Juanita has toured heavily around the country since 2021 headlining and supporting acts like Kaitlin Butts, Braxton Keith, Town Mountain, Nick Shoulders, Emily Nenni, Summer Dean, and Jesse Daniel. Her debut record 'Hardliner' established her reputation as a full-hearted, free-spirited, and irresistibly genuine honky tonk angel. Hannah Juanita's second full length record, 'Tennessee Songbird', produced by Mose Wilson, was released August 30, 2024 to high acclaim, breaking into the top 40 on the Americana Radio Chart and top 3 on the Alt Country Chart. Named one of the five female artists creating the future of country music by Grammy.com, in 2025, Hannah will be touring across America and Europe. THE RESONANT ROGUES On their fourth album, Western North Carolina-based outfit The Resonant Rogues have finally decided to self-title a project. It's a bold move ‚Äî rather like staking a claim on a sound that is both new for them and distinctly their own. From the opening notes of lead track "Sun in Winter," the eponymous record finesses the line between country and soul. The keening of the fiddle and the sway of the pedal steel are classic sounds; the vocals ‚Äî sung by Sparrow who fronts the band with her partner Keith Josiah Smith ‚Äî are poetic and wistful, yet unfussy. "I miss you like the sun in winter / laying in the yard / in the snow / trying to catch that glow / before it goes," she sings. It's a moment encapsulated; something as lovely as it is fleeting. Sparrow and Keith share a passion for movement and sound. Both traveled extensively throughout the U.S. ‚Äî Keith by hopping freight trains, Sparrow with a circus troupe. When the two met by chance in Asheville 10 years ago, they combined their talents and The Resonant Rogues were born. While the band has explored musical styles from across genres and around the globe, current influences for Resonant Rogues, and especially this album, are classic country, Appalachian old-time, and vintage soul. MOSE WILSON

In-Person Connection Practice: Listening
When: Wed, Dec 3, 1:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: SeekHealing Asheville
Tags: Wellness, Spiritual, Community, Support Groups
Description: A Connection Practice is a meeting to practice your skills in listening and connecting with others. No conversation topic is off limits. The only objective of the meeting is to feel a genuine sense of connection by the time it's over, and the only rule is that we promise to not give each other advice.

One seeker always facilitates the meeting (to guide the conversation, manage time, and introduce different exercises to help the group feel connected), and another always volunteers as Space Owl (to step aside with anyone who has a big emotional experience and needs 1-on-1 connection).

There is no hierarchy in Connection Practice meetings, and everyone is encouraged to share equally and freely, including the person who facilitates.

Weekly Critique
When: Wed, Dec 3, 6:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: AVL Writers
Tags: Art, Networking, Book Club, Community
Description: **(Please note the change of venue)**

This is the standing weekly critique at **Westville Pub**. Bring anything new you're working on to share with the group. *If you don't have a project to share, you are most welcome to attend, discuss, and get inspired.*

For our group discussion, please bring at least **8-10 printed copies** of your piece. That way, we can all read through each other's work and provide feedback.

Sharing our creative efforts is an important part of the writing process. I'm really looking forward to reading what you've been working on. Don't worry if it's still a rough draft.

If you're having trouble finding us, look for a placard on the table with the group's name or ask the staff (they will point us out).

**If you would like to join our group email list for updates regarding contests, events, and to request to join the group Discord, you can [sign up on our website](https://avlwriters.com/).**

Description: Join Us for Bluegrass Wednesdays with the Saylor Brothers!

Jam \> Grass \> Jam with the Saylor Brothers \+ special guests happens at French Broad River Brewery every Wednesday night from 6:30 ‚Äì 8:30 pm! This bluegrass jam is led by Ben and Will Saylor and Greg Stiglets, with a rotating cast of special guests, making each week is different and unique.

This is a free show, with no cover charge. 

The Saylor Brothers are a jamgrass fusion group from Asheville, North Carolina fronted by brothers Will & Ben Saylor, of Brushfire Stankgrass. This project is a foray further into the realm of bluegrass jam, with more emphasis on improvisation piled on top of a structure of traditional bluegrass and innovative original songwriting. As a trio with Greg Stiglets on bass, the band packs a large sound coming from three acoustic instruments, and often adds a fourth and fifth player for further improvisational and bluegrass firepower.

Bonnie ‚ÄúPrince‚Äù Billy
When: Wed, Dec 3, 8:00 PM
Where: The Grey Eagle
Price: $37.96
Host: The Grey Eagle
Tags: Live Music, Family
Description: ALL AGESSTANDING ROOM ONLY BONNIE "PRINCE" BILLY The human who sings and composes under the name Bonnie "Prince" Billy and acts under the name Will Oldham has, over the past three-plus decades, made an idiosyncratic journey through, and an indelible mark on, the worlds of independent music and cinema. With his highly individualistic approach to music making and the music industry, one that cherishes intimacy, community, mystery, and spontaneity; his brilliance has captivated fans and made Bonny one of our most influential and beloved songsmiths.Bonnie "Prince" Billy's latest offerings include 2023's Keeping Secrets Will Destroy You and 2024's Hear the Children Sing the Evidence (with Nathan Salsburg and Tyler Trotter). He had a cameo role in Jeff Nichols' The Bikeriders. BPB's newest record is The Purple Bird (produced by David Ferguson), and features such giants of American music as John Anderson and Tim O'Brien. MATT KIVEL Matt Kivel is a songwriter based in Austin, Texas. He has released 7 full length albums. His music has received acclaim from "critics" and audiences all over the world. Not that long ago he played a sold out concert in Tokyo and couldn't believe that people showed up. It was incredible. His music plays with form and the songs take on many different shapes. Sometimes they are loud and distorted, echoing into a mesmerizing drone; other times they are extremely quiet‚Äîlike the deathbed confession of an old tycoon who's got one last secret to share before the buzzards pick his bones clean. And other times, they are fun, warm, and warped: insular transmissions that bring to mind the tunes of slick songwriters like Ric Ocasek and Jackson Brown. Regardless, you'll get the hang of it once you hear it. Trust me.

Thursday Run

Where: Arden, NC
Price: Free
Host: Asheville Runners
Tags: Fitness, Outdoors, Beer
Description: Come run 1, 3, or 6 miles and stay for a beer and soccer tennis after at Olde London Road.

Routes-
1 miler:
RIGHT out of OLR parking lot
Continue around roundabout at Clingman, and head toward the river on Lyman St.
RIGHT on River Arts Place
Cross Riverside onto the Greenway
Right on the Greenway to the Craven St Park put in (the dock)
Turn around and go back the same way to OLR

3 miler:
Start the same as 1 miler
Continue onto Craven St. Bridge
LEFT onto Greenway after bridge
Follow Greenway all the way until it ends at Haywood Rd.
RIGHT onto Haywood Rd, go across the bridge
Cross the Roundabout at Roberts St. and continue onto Clingman
Continue on Clingman
LEFT onto Owens Bell Lane
LEFT onto Hilliard at the top of the hill
LEFT onto W Haywood, follow all the way down to Roberts
LEFT onto Roberts
Follow Roberts back to OLR
Pass OLR to Bartlett, turn around and come back to OLR

6 miler:
After the W Haywood downhill to Roberts
LEFT onto Roberts St. take to Lyman and head back to the Greenway
LEFT onto the Greenway, take all the way to Amboy
RIGHT on Amboy to cross the bridge
RIGHT into French Broad River Park, run the loop at the park
Cross back over the bridge on Amboy and run the Greenway back to the roundabout
Follow Lyman back to OLR

Inquiry in Motion: Open Floor Movement Class Series
When: Thu, Dec 4, 6:30 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: $130
Host: Asia House
Tags: Dance, Fitness, Wellness, Spiritual
Description: **The series is 6 weeks of dancing with the same group of people. Each week we will explore a different theme, which we will be able to integrate into our everyday lives.**

**Pre-registration is required.**

**Visit the following link to find out the dates of the next series: http://www.staceybutcher.com/inquiry-in-motion-committed-series-in-asheville.html**

Join us as we embark on a dynamic moving exploration of the truth that resides in our own body. Through the Open Floor movement/dance practice, Somatic Experiencing principles, and mindful inquiry, we will journey below the stories about who we are and who we should be. Together we will strengthen our skills to listen, track and follow the innate wisdom of our own body, discovering how it speaks to us through movement.

Open Floor is a healing movement meditation practice and lively dance inquiry. The emphasis is to awaken our sensate experience, emotional intelligence, relational skills, and mindful awareness. From our practice on the dance floor, you will develop greater trust in your body's natural intelligence that will enable you to live with more awareness, vitality and joy.

Advantages of dancing with a committed group: ‚Ä¢ We meet with the same group each week. ‚Ä¢ We develop a safe container in which we can dive deeper together over time. ‚Ä¢ We develop trust in our community.

\~~~~~~

‚ÄúWOW! Stacey's Open Floor Movement dance workshops are my favorite thing in life right now! She hosts a closed cohort that meets for 5 or 6 weeks at a time. There's true healing here! Stacey also brings her depth of somatic knowledge into the curated workshops that feel to be a melding between somatic experiencing, yoga, and ceremony. Of all the conscious dance in Asheville, what Stacey has created is truly unique, special, intentional, and EXACTLY the space you want to be in if you desire movement for healing mind, body, and soul!‚Äù ~ Jessica R.

PERFORMANCE: Tesla Quartet: The Music of Hugo Kauder
When: Thu, Dec 4, 7:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: $10
Host: Black Mountain College Museum + Arts Center 
Tags: Live Music, Art, Education
Description: **PERFORMANCE: The Music of Hugo Kauder**

**Thursday, December 4th, 2025 at 7pm**

**Black Mountain College Museum + Arts Center {120 College Street}**

**TICKETS ‚Äì $15 General Admission / $10 for BMCM+AC Members + Students w/ ID**

BMCM+AC is excited to welcome back The Tesla Quartet! This special performance, presented in conjunction with our¬†*Points in Space*¬†exhibition, will bring to life the music of Hugo Kauder, who served as composer-in-residence at Black Mountain College during the summer of 1945. The program will feature Kauder‚Äôs¬†*Seventh String Quartet*, the same work first performed at BMC in 1945, offering audiences a rare chance to experience this historic piece in a contemporary setting.

"***From the outset, the quartet plays as a single instrument. Their sound is balanced across registers, their timbres and articulations matched." -The Classic Review***

The Tesla Quartet is known the world over for their ‚Äúsuperb capacity to find the inner heart of everything they play, regardless of era, style, or technical demand‚Äù (*The International Review of Music*). From cutting-edge contemporary works to established masterpieces, the Tesla Quartet‚Äôs emotive and thoughtful interpretations reveal the ensemble‚Äôs deep commitment to the craft and to their ever-expanding repertoire. The quartet recognizes the power of their platform to amplify underrepresented voices and to encourage the proliferation of an equitable and just future for society as well as a hospitable climate for posterity.

The Tesla Quartet is Ross Snyder (violin), Michelle Lie (violin), Edwin Kaplan (viola), and Austin Fisher (cello).

\_\_\_

Hugo Kauder devoted his life to composing, teaching, playing, and writing about music. A successful early career in Vienna abruptly ended with the annexation of Austria into Nazi Germany. Kauder left Austria for Holland in 1938, thanks to a contract with Dutch publisher NV Mees Uitgeverij to produce settings of poems by Albert Verway. After a stop in England, Kauder settled in New York City in 1940. During Kauder‚Äôs short stay in Holland (1938-39), he formed a lasting friendship with the musicologist Edward Lowinsky, who also came to the United States and became a professor of music at Black Mountain College (1942-47). One of the era‚Äôs most prolific chamber music composers, Kauder wrote over 200 instrumental works, including 10 concertos and concert pieces (2 each for oboe, piano and violin, 1 each for cello, horn and viola, and a double concerto for violin and viola), 5 symphonies, 19 string quartets, 11 piano trios, 2 piano quartets, and variations for piano quintet. He also composed over 100 vocal works, including choral music for various combinations, an opera (Merlin), and a large number of art songs with piano (or other instruments). At a time when many believed that Western tonality had run its course, Kauder developed a style that, rather than denying, expanded the concept of traditional tonality.

Visitor's Center toward Highway 25
When: Fri, Dec 5, 9:00 AM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: Asheville Mountains-to-Sea Trail Hiking Club 2.0
Tags: Fitness, Outdoors, Pets
Description: This is a fairly easy hike, and we go at a high average to low advanced speed, which is roughly about 3.0 to 3.2 mph. There are no super long hills. It's pretty undulating all the way.

Well behaved dogs on leashes are welcome to attend.

When you arrive, park near the woods close to where the kiosk is at the trailhead.

Mountains-to-Sea-Trail hikes are designed for fitness and community among people who are already reasonably fit. It's not an endurance hike by any means, but it is designed so we can get our hearts beating a bit while still being able to have a conversation and meet new people.
When you arrive, we'll circle up and introduce ourselves briefly. There will be a person who is a sweep. This person is the person who walks last and makes sure no one gets lost.

We leave the parking spot at 9:10. If someone needs a nature break, we wait fo you, but it's not a hike where we stop and take photos or frequent breaks. We basically keep hiking until the 1/2 way mark, then turn around after a short (approximately 5 minute) break. Then we keep that same pace on the way back. If we get on a trail right at 9:10, we are normally finished around 10:50.

These are out and back hikes, meaning that we hike in and turn around half way to return back.

Melissa Joiner
When: Fri, Dec 5, 6:00 PM
Where: 55 College Street
Asheville, NC  28801
Price: Unknown
Host: Asheville Music Hall & The One Stop
Tags: Live Music, Nightlife
Description: Melissa Joiner
Doors: 5:00 PM 

Hailing from the Gulf Coast of Alabama, internationally touring singer-songwriter Melissa Joiner has been immersed in music since birth. 
Her creative use of formal opera training and Delta Blues influence has created a diverse style that has made her a standout. 
Melissa grew up singing in a world famous Roadhouse on the Florida/Alabama line and cut her teeth in some of the last Juke Joints in Mississippi. 
 
After reaching her goal of playing 30 countries by the age of 30, Melissa decided to call the East Coast home. 
Her music can be heard on radio stations, at festivals, and at shows all over the world.
 
Recently, Melissa released an album called Changing, had a song chart at number one in Norway, has had multiple cuts from signed artists, 
and has toured in Nicaragua, Costa Rica, Portugal, and Hawaii. To learn more and hear her music, check out www.melissajoinermusic.com

Purchase Tickets: https://www.etix.com/ticket/servlet/s/38218505

Soft fuzziest of sweaters
To be a warm embrace

Like the temperature of tea

Like the tropics sand & seas

Too many hearts on hold

About AMC:
Asheville Movement Collective envisions a world that moves in harmony where all are free to be their authentic selves within a loving community. Southern Culture on the Skids
When: Fri, Dec 5, 8:00 PM
Where: The Grey Eagle
Price: $27.06
Host: The Grey Eagle
Tags: Live Music, Family
Description: ALL AGESSTANDING ROOM ONLY SOUTHERN CULTURE ON THE SKIDS Southern Culture On The Skids has been consistently recording and touring around the world since 1983. The band (Rick Miller ‚Äì guitar and vocals, Mary Huff ‚Äì bass and vocals, Dave Hartman ‚Äì drums) has been playing together for over 30 years. Their musical journey has taken them from all-night North Carolina house parties to late night TV talk shows (Conan O'Brien, The Tonight Show), from performing at the base of Mt. Fuji in Japan to rockin' out for the inmates at North Carolina correctional facilities. They've shared a stage with many musical luminaries including Link Wray, Loretta Lynn, Hasil Adkins and Patti Smith. Their music has been featured in movies and TV, parodied by Weird Al, and used to sell everything from diamonds to pork sausage. In 2014 the band was honored by the Southern Folklife Collection at the University of North Carolina Chapel Hill with an exhibition featuring their music and cultural contributions. Their legendary live shows are a testament to the therapeutic powers of foot-stomping, butt-shaking rock and roll and what Rolling Stone dubbed "a hell raising rock and roll party." At Home with Southern Culture on the Skids is the latest full length album from the band and was released in March of 2021. It was recorded during the stay at home period of the pandemic when the band was at home and not touring. The album consists of 11 tracks recorded and mixed in Rick Miller's living room with some additional tracks recorded at his studio, The Kudzu Ranch. The first radio single off the album is "Run Baby Run"‚Äîa rocking number with deep garage roots. SCOTS bassist Mary Huff provides an urgent vocal while the band pulls back the throttle on a full race fuzz fest‚Äîcause she's gotta to go fast! Run Baby Run! The other songs on the album are a combination of the band's unique mix of musical genres: rock and roll, surf, folk and country‚Äîall a bit off-center, what Rick proudly calls "our wobbly Americana". Rick goes on, "We put a few more acoustic guitars on this one, as you would expect if you recorded in your living room, but it still rocks like SCOTS. So put your headphones on, get in your favorite chair/sofa/recliner, put on "At Home With" and let's hang out for a while." PLEASURE CHEST Blues, soul, rock & roll from Asheville, NC. Funky but chic SINCE 2012

12 Bars of Christmas
When: Sat, Dec 6, 12:00 AM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: The Funkatorium
Tags: Holiday, Beer, Wine & Spirits, Nightlife, Tours, Markets
Description: This holiday season, Asheville locals and visitors are invited to sip, stroll, and support a great cause with the launch of the 12 Bars of Christmas, a citywide holiday collaboration benefiting MANNA FoodBank. The event brings together beloved local bars, festive spirits, & generous hearts to help fight hunger across WNC while also offering a meaningful way to support businesses still recovering from Helene.

HOW IT WORKS

Participants can join the fun by visiting any participating venue and making a $15 donation to receive their official 12 Bars of Christmas Passport. 100% of all passport proceeds go directly to MANNA FoodBank, whose mission is to involve, educate, and unite people in the fight to end hunger in WNC.

With a passport in hand, the holiday adventure begins. Guests collect a stamp while visiting each of the 12 participating bars, and those who complete all 12 stamps will receive a 2025 limited-edition keepsake ornament to celebrate their community spirit (while supplies last). It‚Äôs a chance to explore Asheville‚Äôs vibrant bar scene, enjoy festive specials, and show love to local businesses working hard to bounce back this season.

Participants can also submit their passport‚Äôs entry form at any bar for a chance to win big in the¬†12 Bars of Christmas Charity Raffle, with a live drawing on¬†January 6.

Points in Space: Performance at Black Mountain College Exhibit
When: Sat, Dec 6, 11:00 AM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: Black Mountain College Museum + Arts Center
Tags: Art, Theater & Film, Education, Community
Description: Black Mountain College‚Äôs interdisciplinary and collaborative philosophy fostered groundbreaking time-based experiments across disciplines, significantly influencing performance, theater, film, music, dance, and visual art worldwide.¬†*Points in Space: Performance at Black Mountain College*¬†will feature¬†visual and time-based artworks that echo BMC‚Äôs innovative spirit from 1933 to 1957.¬†BMC was a nexus of avant-garde activity, fostering innovation through collaboration and experiential learning. The exhibition will highlight key events and figures, such as John Cage, Merce Cunningham, Lou Harrison, Roland Hayes, Ray Johnson, Hugo Kauder, Ursula Mamlok, Robert Rauschenberg, David Tudor, Alma Stone Williams, Stan Vanderbeek, and Stefan Wolpe, alongside movements like Bauhaus, Dada, and Fluxus. The exhibition will feature historical and contemporary works, interactive installations, performances, and immersive experiences that bring the past into conversation with the present.

*Points in Space*¬†aims to bridge the past and present, ensuring BMC‚Äôs interdisciplinary spirit continues to inspire new generations. Through performance-integrated exhibitions and public programs, the exhibition will foster a dynamic dialogue between historical and contemporary artistic practices, expanding the reach and relevance of BMC‚Äôs radical approach to art, education, and community engagement.

Read more about featured artists in this exhibition on our website.

*Points in Space: Performance at Black Mountain College*¬†is organized by Jeff Arnal, curator, and Adolfo Alzuphar, curatorial assistant.

Coptic Book Making Workshop
When: Sat, Dec 6, 12:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Unknown
Host: The North Carolina Arboretum
Tags: Crafts, Education
Description: Coptic Book Making Workshop

with Joyce Tromba 

Saturday, December 6¬† |¬† 12 ‚Äì 4 pm 

REGISTER HERE 

The Coptic stitch bookbinding was first used in Egypt by the Copts in the 2nd Century AD. It has become popular again with hand bookmakers because of the beauty of it‚Äôs exposed spine as well as the structure of the book which allows it to open flat. In this class we will use the twin needle technique to sew the binding.¬† 

This is a perfect sized book to keep with you for notes or sketches and would also make a lovely gift. 

All materials will be provided, including a selection of papers for the covers and optional signature wraps but if you have some special paper you would like to use for the covers please contact me at joycetromba@gmail.com so I can give you advice about size and grain direction. 

Joyce Tromba is happily settled into life in lovely Western North Carolina after living and teaching around the world for 30 years. Her travels have exposed her to many fiber traditions and she has always found groups of fiber folks wherever she was to share her making with. Joyce has 20\+ years teaching design, sewing, knitting, quilting and bookmaking to High School students and adults. She has studied fiber and book and fiber arts at Penland, Arrowmont, John C. Campbell Folk School, and the Center for Book Arts in New York City. Her work can be found at Local Cloth where she also teaches natural dyeing, bookmaking and sewing classes. 

Members: Remember to enter your promo code upon checkout to receive your 10% member discount! Email adulteducation@ncarboretum.org with questions.

See a full listing of Adult Education Programs at the North Carolina Arboretum here! Questions? Check our FAQs.

We are committed to fostering a diverse, supportive learning community. If the cost of a class is a barrier for you, please complete this scholarship form and we will see what kind of assistance we can provide.

Follow us on Facebook & Instagram!

Join our Adult Education Student Hub on Discord!

Interested in supporting the NC Arboretum more directly? Donate to the ONE Fund here.

See all of our classes open for registration here!

Adult Studio‚ÄîBaskets: Weaving Tradition and Today
When: Sat, Dec 6, 1:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Unknown
Host: AVL Today
Tags: Crafts, Education, Art
Description: Join us for an engaging, hands-on introduction to the art of basket weaving. In this beginner-friendly class, participants will learn the fundamental weaving techniques needed to create their own simple basket. Along the way, we‚Äôll explore the rich history and cultural significance of basketry among the Cherokee and other Indigenous peoples across the United States. We‚Äôll discuss how this traditional craft has evolved over time and how it continues to thrive in today‚Äôs world as both a functional art form and a means of cultural preservation. No prior experience is necessary, just curiosity and a willingness to learn! All materials will be provided. 

Artist Bio: 

Bryanna Weavers‚Äô work explores the intersections of culture, memory, and identity through the lens of archaeology and Indigenous heritage. Bryanna seeks to create visual narratives that honor ancestral knowledge while inviting contemporary audiences to reflect on their connection to the past. Each piece aims to bridge history and modernity, encouraging dialogue about preservation, resilience, and belonging. 

Adult Studio:

Local and visiting artists help students of all levels and abilities develop skills in media that reflect techniques and themes featured in the Museum‚Äôs Collection and special exhibitions. Classes are designed for anyone interested in exploring specific media in depth or introduce new media and processes.

Winter Buds & Bark Tree ID
When: Sat, Dec 6, 1:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Unknown
Host: The North Carolina Arboretum
Tags: Outdoors, Education, Tours
Description: Winter Buds & Bark Tree ID

with Lauren Lampley 

Saturday, December 6¬† |¬† 1 ‚Äì 4 pm 

BRN ‚Äì Core¬† |¬† BREG ‚Äì Elective 

REGISTER HERE 

Ever wondered how you can identify a tree without its leaves? All tree species have different patterns of bark and leaf/flower buds that can be used to identify them even in winter time. In this program, we will look closely at the common trees around the NC Arboretum trails and point out specific characteristics of their buds and bark so you can identify them even without their leaves. 

This program will take place outside and will follow easy trails and paved walkways. Dress for the weather and prepare to be outside for the entire program time. 

Lauren Lampley began her career at Grandfather Mountain Stewardship Foundation as a Park Naturalist which solidified Lauren‚Äôs interests in ecology and a passion for teaching others. She has led walks and hikes in a variety of subjects from Geology to Birding and especially likes to learn and teach about our local ecology. She currently works at the NC Arboretum in the Adult Education Department and manages the Blue Ridge Naturalist Certificate of Merit.

MELISSA CARPER "I don't think you can get this sound unless it's borned in ya," said bluegrass legend Ralph Stanley, when asked about what he called "old-time mountain music." When Melissa Carper heard those words, something jumped inside her. While staying in the country with a friend, she found an old DVD of Down From the Mountain, the documentary and concert film of the "O, Brother Where Art Thou'' soundtrack that featured this particular Stanley interview. She immediately jotted down "borned in ya" on a piece of paper. "I knew I had to write that song," she recalls. In the Spring of 2023, Carper went back to East Nashville's Bomb Shelter ‚Äì the same "analog wonderland" where she'd recorded Ramblin' Soul and its predecessor, Daddy's Country Gold, and enlisted the help of her trusted co-producers ‚Äì Dennis Crouch and Andrija Tokic. "Borned In Ya" would become the title track of the new album, out July 19th via Mae Music/Thirty Tigers.

Mizzo: When someone mentions the name 'Mizzo', the first thing that comes to mind is groovy, infectious rhythms with lots of bass. There isn't anyone more passionate about rocking dance floors than Mizzo. With the love of high energy rhythms combined with the addiction of introducing new music to his friends, Mizzo got his first taste of DJ'ing back in 2001 when he bought a pair of used turntables and a mixer from a local pawn shop. He taught himself how to mix and has not looked back since. Born in Winston Salem, Mizzo continues to call North Carolina his home. Well known for his work as resident DJ at Greene Street Nightclub and Limelight respectively, Mizzo has gained appeal from the masses and has taken nightlife to another level. After years of being one of the Triad's top DJs, Mizzo had to move to a city growing as quickly as his DJ career. Immediately after relocating to Charlotte, Mizzo was able to establish himself as one of the city's most requested DJs. Mizzo holds residencies at venues in multiple cities throughout NC. Having played private parties for a few celebrities, he is quickly gaining recognition all over the east coast. Known for dropping bass heavy anthems from club to club, Mizzo early on caught the attention of several promoters and landed gigs as direct support for artists such as Stanton Warriors, DJ Icey, Two Friends, Keith Mackenzie, Mafia Kiss, RAC, Dieselboy, Caked Up, Lo IQ and more. Fast forward to today, Mizzo is headlining venues throughout the United States with international bookings on the horizon.

Malfunkshun: Born and raised in Miami. MalFunkShun is the genre-blending solo project of Charlotte-based producer Jorge Ramirez. From small dark clubs to massive outdoor festivals, MalFunkShun is always turning it out. DJ/ Producer and overall hustler of the beats. Banging out a soundtrack of underground party music. His ability to seamlessly mix booty, breaks, hip hop, and house into hard-hitting club-shakers has become his trademark booty bass sound. ‚ÄúIf this don't make your booty move, your booty must be dead.‚Äù

About AMC:
Asheville Movement Collective envisions a world that moves in harmony where all are free to be their authentic selves within a loving community. Our mission and aim are to inspire authenticity and healthy community through free-form dance by hosting dance waves for personal and community transformation. AMC is a 501(c)(3) nonprofit organization.

üíª >>hack day<< Marketing for Makers: Organic Growth Hacks
When: Sun, Dec 7, 10:00 AM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: AVL Digital Nomads
Tags: Networking, Crafts
Description: *Forget tutorials. Learn by doing. We‚Äôll start with five minutes of vibecoding tips, then spend the morning building whatever your imagination (and AI) can handle.*

üìà **Sunday, December 7 ¬∑ 10am‚Äì1pm**

**Bring a laptop + tiny idea = Leave with users (or at least a plan)**

***

**üí≠ What We‚Äôre Doing**
We‚Äôre keeping the same format: short talk, long build.
This time we‚Äôre talking about what happens *after* you ship.

**Then you‚Äôll get two solid hours to build literally *whatever you want* using those tips as your playbook.**

**‚ÄúMarketing for Makers: Organic Growth Hacks‚Äù** is about getting eyes on what you build without being cringe, pushy, or paying for ads.

You don‚Äôt need a huge audience or a marketing degree. You just need the right habits and tools.

We‚Äôll do a mini-presentation on organic reach, growth loops, and social proof, then everyone gets time to promote, tweak, or prep their next launch.

Vibecoding = you describe what you want ‚Üí AI builds the scaffolding ‚Üí you guide it to greatness.

And sometimes, that greatness comes from distribution.

***

**üéô Mini Talk: Organic Growth Hacks That Work**

1Ô∏è‚É£ *Build in public* ‚Äì Share your process, not just your product.
2Ô∏è‚É£ *Tell a story* ‚Äì People follow stories, not features.
3Ô∏è‚É£ *Use loops* ‚Äì Create something people can share or remix.
4Ô∏è‚É£ *Ask, then iterate* ‚Äì Real feedback beats endless building.
5Ô∏è‚É£ *Post fast, fix later* ‚Äì Momentum beats polish every time.

We‚Äôll look at real indie creators who got traction without ads and how ‚Äúgrowth hacks‚Äù are really just experiments repeated with consistency.

***

**üéØ What You‚Äôll Actually Do**

**Track 1: ‚ÄúPost It‚Äù**
‚Ä¢ Write a launch tweet, Threads post, or LinkedIn post about your project.
‚Ä¢ Use AI to refine your hook and make it pop.

**Track 2: ‚ÄúSEO It‚Äù**
‚Ä¢ Create a simple landing page or blog post using ChatGPT or Claude.
‚Ä¢ Generate keywords, titles, and meta descriptions instantly.

**Track 3: ‚ÄúLoop It‚Äù**
‚Ä¢ Add one shareable element to your app ‚Äî a button, leaderboard, or generator.
‚Ä¢ Deploy and share your link in the room.

**Bonus Track: ‚ÄúHype It‚Äù**
‚Ä¢ Build a quick pre-launch page with a waitlist or teaser headline.
‚Ä¢ Add a single call-to-action that makes people curious.

***

**ü™© Reality Check**

Marketing isn‚Äôt evil. It‚Äôs storytelling with distribution.
You can‚Äôt help people use what they don‚Äôt know exists.
You don‚Äôt need perfect branding, just clarity and repetition.
We‚Äôll show you how to use small, repeatable actions to build real traction.

\-\-\-

## üõ†Ô∏è Your New Superpowers (The Tools We'll Use)

**For Mobile:**

* **Bolt.new + Expo** ‚Äì Text-to-app that actually works on phones
* **Cursor** ‚Äì Your IDE but with an AI copilot who actually understands context
* **Emergent** ‚Äì AI-powered mobile development platform
* **Rork** ‚Äì Rapid mobile prototyping with AI assistance

**For Web:**

* **Vercel v0.dev** ‚Äì Generates UI components you'd actually want to keep
* **Lovable.dev** ‚Äì Chat your way to full-stack apps
* **Replit Agent** ‚Äì For when you need an AI junior dev for longer tasks

**Command Line tools:**

* **Claude Code** ‚Äì Agentic coding from your terminal with excellent guardrails
* **Gemini CLI** ‚Äì Open-source terminal agent that actually understands your codebase
* **GitHub Copilot CLI** ‚Äì Chat in terminal, ship PRs like a boss
* **OpenAI Codex** ‚Äì Direct access to GPT models for coding workflows

**OR copy/paste from Claude + ChatGPT** ‚Äì Sometimes the simplest solution is the best solution

***

## üìÖ The Plan

**10:00‚Äì10:30 Speed Dating for Ideas**
Pitch your tiny build in 30 seconds. Find your coding buddy. No idea? We have a hat full of them (including "Tinder for finding tennis partners" and "Which friend owes me money tracker").

**10:30‚Äì12:30 The Build Sprint**
Two full hours to build! Pick a track. Steal our prompts. Break things. Fix things. Ship something real. We'll be circulating with "oh wait, try this prompt" tips.

**12:30‚Äì1:00 Victory Lap / Demos**
Show your creation. Share your killer prompt. Drop your deploy link in the chat. Everyone will clap even if it's wonky.

***

## üéí What to Bring

* **Laptop + charger** (mandatory)
* **Headphones** (for focus mode)
* **One tiny idea** (or steal one from our idea jar)
* **Low expectations, high curiosity** (perfect combo)

## ü§ù Who Should Come?

* **Founders / aspiring founders** who want to start working on that business idea
* **Developers** who want to 10x their building speed
* **Designers** who want to make their designs real
* **Product people** who want to test ideas instantly
* **Complete beginners** who think "deploy" is a military term (we'll teach you!)
* **AI skeptics** welcome ‚Äì see what's actually possible vs hype

## üí° You'll Leave With:

‚úÖ A deployed thing you built (with a real URL!)
‚úÖ 3-5 battle-tested prompts you can reuse forever
‚úÖ Actual understanding of how people are shipping with AI today
‚úÖ New friends who also think building stuff is fun
‚úÖ The dangerous confidence to build your next idea

## ‚ö° The Fine Print

**Cost:** Free (bring your own coffee / snacks)
**Skill Level:** "I can open a laptop" to "I deploy to prod on Fridays"
**Mood:** Collaborative chaos with good intentions

Drop us a line in a DM or in a comment down below

Build cool stuff. Help others build cool stuff. Don't be a jerk. That's it.

In-Person Connection Practice
When: Sun, Dec 7, 3:30 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: SeekHealing Asheville
Tags: Wellness, Spiritual, Support Groups
Description: A Connection Practice is a meeting to practice your skills in listening and connecting with others. No conversation topic is off limits. The only objective of the meeting is to feel a genuine sense of connection by the time it's over, and the only rule is that we promise to not give each other advice.

One seeker always facilitates the meeting (to guide the conversation, manage time, and introduce different exercises to help the group feel connected), and another always volunteers as Space Owl (to step aside with anyone who has a big emotional experience and needs 1-on-1 connection).

There is no hierarchy in Connection Practice meetings, and everyone is encouraged to share equally and freely, including the person who facilitates.

Book Club: Why People Believe Weird Things, by Michael Shermer
When: Sun, Dec 7, 4:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: Atheists of WNC
Tags: Networking, Dining, Book Club
Description: **Our next meeting** is **Sunday, December 7, 4 p.m. at Standard Pizza, 755 Biltmore Avenue in Asheville**.

Look for us inside, in the back room.

We will continue our discussion of ***Why People Believe Weird Things: Pseudoscience, Superstition, and Other Confusions of Our Time***, by science writer [Michael Shermer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Shermer). We will focus on Part three, chapters 9 to 11, which is around 45 pages.

From the forward: "Unless we regularly use human reason both to discover and acknowledge nature's factuality, and to follow the logical implications for efficacious human action that such knowledge entails, we will lose out to the frightening forces of irrationality, romanticism, uncompromising "true"belief, and the apparent resulting inevitability of mob action. Skepticism is the agent of reason against organized irrationalism and is therefore one of the keys to human social and civic decency."

Note: Each section stands alone and is prime for discussion, so newcomers are welcome!
We would like to keep each meeting to a max of 10 people. **Please RSVP** if you do plan to come.

**Our Mission Statement**
This is a group of Loving and Light oriented individuals coming together to support each other, ourselves, and our local and global community in these current challenging and transformational times.

1. **We recognize that Earth has now begun a global transformation that has been the center of much discussion and preparation for many, many years and in many cultures.**
a. Acknowledging and reviewing past information and references that point to and discuss this current global transformation.
2. **We recognize that our ability to shape the unfolding of our reality is far beyond what we have imagined (especially at this time!)**
a. Acknowledging and reviewing the current information on the Earth‚Äôs recent and ongoing rise in her vibratory frequency and the resulting effect on accelerated manifestation.
b. Reviewing, exploring, and discussing how manifested reality is created, including the information revealed through Quantum Mechanics.
c. Creating through love and unity consciousness vs creating from fear and separation consciousness.
3. **And we recognize the importance of embodying and bringing into our personal lives and, therefore, into the global consciousness uplifting, healing, empowering, and transformational energies.**
a. Raising our vibratory frequency through experiencing a variety of meditations designed to deepen the embodied realization of the clear light of consciousness as the true essence of ourselves, all beings, and manifested reality.
4. **We also recognize that "spiritual by passing", or avoiding and ignoring our's and other's human challenges, problems, and suffering, may not be ultimately helpful, compassionate, or responsible. Therefore, for those of us who are moved to reach out into the greater community, we will explore skillful ways to engage in appropriate community outreach and action.**
a. Developing the skill of communicating and acting from Heart Wisdom and Unity Consciousness while interacting with unawakened aspects of ourselves as well as within individuals and communities under the current spell of separation (fear/control) conscious.
b. Skillful ways we can support and express our values of compassion, care, and truth in our current political climate WITHOUT contributing to the negativity, fear, anger, and separation consciousness that is currently exerting its power to control.

**Through meditations, presentations, and individual sharing and group discussions we will receive and give more light, wisdom, love, and support than may be available to us on our own.**

*It is time to come together and co-create and actively invite into manifested reality the world we will know as our true home. The home that reflects who we truly are! This is both our invitation and our delight!*

**SHARED AGREEMENTS for the group: Asheville Lightworkers Collaborative**
*By participating in this Asheville Lightworkers Collaborative group, I agree to:*

1. **Share within the framework of the group‚Äôs agreed mission.** We will explore how to consciously be, express, and demonstrate the Truth of who we are - and how we may support one another to be the change we wish to experience in our world as well as skillfully uplift any endeavor we would like to bring to our local and global communities. And, if we would like to share anything that may not directly relate to the group's mission, we will keep it at a minimum unless it is directly related to what we are discussing.
2. **I agree to practice good communication skills.**
I agree to listen deeply whenever another member of the group is sharing ‚Äì
with the intention to fully understand, refraining from thinking about how I might
respond until that person is completely finished with his/her sharing. And, whenever a problem or challenge arises amongst us, I speak up about this in a way that expresses the problem courteously and non-blamefully. In such situations, I look first to observe my own behavior to discover if I may have contributed in any way to the challenge.
3. **I agree to keep my first attention on my own inner and outer experience,** **ideas and concerns by**:
(a) Keeping my shares focused on the mission of the group and to support and encourage other group members rather than give advice or try to fix other‚Äôs problems. And, I agree to support and encourage the purpose of the group and to refrain from offering an opinion on any aspect of their sharing unless specifically requested.
(b) Being 100% committed to my own expression as a Light Worker in the world.
4. **In stepping into this commitment, I agree to refrain from duo purposes such as marketing my business or pursuing someone in the group because of a romantic interest.** This maintains the cohesiveness and integrity of the group and its mission.
5. **I agree to take full responsibility for my own wellbeing as I engage with this group.**
I realize that, although what we do and explore in this group can be transformative in nature, it is not a substitute for therapeutic assistance. Should I find myself having difficulty abiding by the shared agreements for this group, or if I am experiencing a personal life crisis that I am having difficulty navigating alone, I agree to be responsible for generating any additional support that I might need rather than expecting this group to provide the extra support I am needing.
6. **I agree to honor and respect the group members.**
I agree to be respectful and honoring of other group members at all times, as well as protective of the safety and sacredness of our circle by refraining from gossip and agreeing to never diminish any other person in our group ‚Äì during circle gatherings or outside of them.

*We share gratitude with Thriving Loving Relationships for use of this agreement*

Dec 7th An evening of Sensual Snuggles for Poly/ENM folks
When: Sun, Dec 7, 6:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: Asheville Cuddle Collective
Tags: Wellness, LGBTQ+, Community, Education
Description: Please note- If you want to attend this event you need to purchase a ticket- We advertise in many places and only paid tickets will reserve your space. https://www.zeffy.com/en-US/ticketing/dec-7th-polyenm-sensual-snuggle

**This event is specifically for people who identify as or are curious about poly and ENM relationship.**

**What is a Sensual Snuggle Event?**
This is a sweet & welcoming event where we practice and use verbal consent to connect and share touch. We talk about boundaries and practice both saying and receiving a ‚Äúno‚Äù. In this space it is common to see people cuddle, share massage, have their hair brushed, kiss, expose nipples, play, laugh, cry, and be vulnerable. This is a sober space where we can relax and connect with other humans who are seeking touch based connection.
We strive for this to be a safe event. Safe touch enhances our ability to connect with and trust people. When we are in a space of safety, we are able to relax, feel comfort, and be vulnerable.

**Our Agreements:**
1- We ask for what we want an wait for a yes before touching others.
2- We say no if we don‚Äôt want to do something.
3- We try to receive a no with grace and not take it personally.
4- We arrive on time, clean (as scent free as possible), and sober.
5- We keep our pants/shorts on at this event. (Tops are optional; this is a sensual space, not a sexual space.)
6- We are here to connect with others. Connection can be verbal, platonic, or spicy!
7- We welcome diversity. Isms and Phobias are not welcome here!

**Who should attend:**
People who are interested in safely exploring touch and sensuality with strangers. This includes people who are single, people who are not single, couples, folks who are new to town and looking for connection, people of all/any genders and sexual orientations, people of all ages (18 and up). People who understand and respect consent, who will take care of themselves and people around them. This event is queer-normative. The guest list will include all genders, orientations, ages, and personalities. If that‚Äôs not your thing‚Ä¶ This is not the event for you.
***Who should NOT attend:***
-People who are only looking for a sex party.
-People who do not understand and respect consent.
-People who have extreme fear of setting and speaking their personal boundaries; in order to create a safe space we need to know that you will say ‚Äúno‚Äù if you feel a no.
-People who are homophobic, racist, sexist, ageist, ableist‚Ä¶
-People under 18 years of age.
***Schedule of the Evening***

* 6:45pm Doors Open, Mix & Mingle
* 7:00pm We gather in a circle to meet each other, build a container, cover consent and boundary setting and discuss event agreements. Then we will play a few intimacy building games to meet and connect with other people in the room. Please make sure you arrive on-time!
* 8:15pm Once the container is built we will have self directed snuggling and sensual interactions until the end of the party.
* 10:50pm Closing Circle; a time to re-center and connect as a group to verbally share anything that came up at the event or to voice gratitude to someone(s) you enjoyed interacting with.
* 11:00pm cleanup & head home; you are welcome to help.

**We take individual and group safety seriously!** If you experience, see, or know that one of our participants is not safe to be at this event we want to know about it. We are committed to doing our best to create a safe environment which means that if someone is causing harm (physical or mental) that person is not welcome here (this includes harm that takes place outside of our events). We stand behind survivors and know that some of our participants are here to heal from touch based trauma.

These events are not "gender balanced"[. Check out our website for more information about this decision. ](http://holdmeavl.com/why-i-dont-gender-balance-events/)

**Simple definitions/clarifications-** Platonic- marked by the absence of romance or sex.
Most of the interactions we have with friends and strangers are platonic.
Sensual- gratification of the senses or the indulgence of appetite.
We might feel sensual when we feel someone's breath on our neck or experience a extra long and slow caress.
Sexual- having or involving sex.
Often involving one more more peoples genitals; perhaps seeking orgasm.
\*Refund Policy- Full refund if you cancel 7 days before the event or you cancel due to illness, emergency, or direct exposure to covid. Credit towards a future event if you cancel more than 3 days before an event. No refund if you cancel within 2 days of the event or no-show.

Robert Lester Folsom
When: Sun, Dec 7, 8:00 PM
Where: The Grey Eagle
Price: $29.75
Host: The Grey Eagle
Tags: Live Music, Family
Description: ALL AGESSTANDING ROOM ONLY ROBERT LESTER FOLSOM Robert Lester Folsom is a Georgia-born singer-songwriter and guitarist whose music blends soft psych, Americana, and sun-faded AM gold into a sound unmistakably his own. First self-released in 1976, his cult-classic LP Music and Dreams quietly circulated in the Southeast before slipping into obscurity‚Äîuntil crate diggers and reissue labels revived his recordings in the 2010s. The album was re-released in 2014 by Anthology Recordings (a Mexican Summer imprint), bringing Folsom's homegrown vision to a new generation of listeners. Following that rediscovery, Folsom's previously unheard material was brought to light through Ode to a Rainy Day: Archives 1972‚Äì1975 and Sunshine Only Sometimes: Archives Vol. 2‚Äîtwo acclaimed compilations of heartfelt demos that deepened his reputation as a lost master of homespun pop. A wave of younger fans has discovered Folsom's music through Instagram, TikTok, and sync placements in hit shows like Outer Banks and Gossip Girl. After only a handful of rare appearances over the years, he's now riding that resurgence‚Äîactively touring and performing to packed rooms nationwide, including a sold-out night at The Troubadour and a celebrated set at Newport Folk Festival. Folsom's latest archival single, "Sitting on the Moon," is out now as part of Mexican Summer's latest eponymous compilation, offering yet another lost gem from this storied vault. A third full-length collection of archival material, Archives Vol. 3, is slated for release in 2026.

Holiday: Mini Grove Loop and Gingerbread Houses
When: Mon, Dec 8, 5:45 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: The Asheville Hiking Group
Tags: Holiday, Outdoors, Tours
Description: **Rating:** Moderate
**Distance:** 4 miles
**Elevation Gain:** 750 ish
**Surface:** Road
**Pace:** 3.2 mph on road, strolling through Grove Park Inn.
**Features:** This hike will have an abbreviated Grove Park Loop with a stop in the Grove Park Inn to see the Gingerbread Houses
**Bears:** Not likely
**Dogs:** No Dogs are allowed in the Grove Park. If you want to bring them, you can, but you won't be able to go inside to see the Gingerbread Houses.
**Gear:** Cash/Payment for beverage inside the Grove Park Inn, if you wish. Headlamp or Flashlight to light your way.

**Meeting Spot is Beth Israel - don't trust the pin on the map. it's stuck:** [https://maps.app.goo.gl/6NQA64Xak3KaFHGr8](https://maps.app.goo.gl/6NQA64Xak3KaFHGr8)

**Route:**
Weaver Park on Murdock Road, Up through Griffing Rose Garden, Up Griffing Blvd to Sunset, Down to Grove Park Inn, back to Weaver Park.

This excursion was suggested by Kimberly K. If you have an excursion you'd like to suggest, please let me know.

**Scenic Asheville Series:** Not part of the series.

**RSVP and On-Time Start:**

* If you decide you cannot come, please change your RSVP
* There are generally 1 or 2 no-shows on my hikes, so we don't wait for people to arrive. If you are late, you'll be left behind. In some hikes, there are "if late" instructions to intercept us.
* Notes and comments are genuinely appreciated.

***No Guests***: Please ask guests to sign up for the hike themselves.

The organizer of this trip is a volunteer and not a professional guide. The function of the organizer is only to organize this trip. Description: For our next book club, we will be discussing North Woods by Daniel Mason. We will attempt to return to Zilicoah and see how it goes indoors. There are heaters and a cozy section in the back.

**As we discussed recently, Meetup is charging the fee for running the group again. If you haven't contributed in a while, or feel like you could or want to contribute more, I appreciate any help and whatever you are comfortable with doing! Thank you so much for your help and for continuing to show and up and support the group. I look forward to seeing you at the next meeting. You're welcome to bring cash in person or send to my Venmo whenever! It's Tobias-Roth-2**

The description for the book reads:

A sweeping novel about a single house in the woods of New England, told through the lives of those who inhabit it across the centuries‚Äîa daring, moving tale of memory and fate from the Pulitzer Prize finalist and author of The Piano Tuner and The Winter Soldier.

When a pair of young lovers abscond from a Puritan colony, little do they know that their humble cabin in the woods will become home to an extraordinary succession of inhabitants . An English soldier, destined for glory, abandons the battlefields of the New World to devote himself to apples. A pair of spinster twins survive war and famine, only to succumb to envy and desire. A crime reporter unearths a mass grave, but finds the ancient trees refuse to give up their secrets. A lovelorn painter, a conman, a stalking panther, a lusty beetle; as each one confronts the mysteries of the north woods, they come to realize that the dark, raucous, beautiful past is very much alive.

Traversing cycles of history, nature, and even literature, North Woods shows the myriad, magical ways in which we‚Äôre connected to our environment and to one another, across time, language and space. Written along with the seasons and divided into the twelve months of the year, it is an unforgettable novel about secrets and fates that asks the timeless how do we live on, even after we‚Äôre gone?

Bill Kirchen's Honky Tonk Holiday Show
When: Mon, Dec 8, 6:00 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: $29
Host: The Grey Eagle
Tags: Live Music, Family, Holiday
Description: ALL AGES SEATED SHOW LIMITED NUMBER OF PREMIUM SEATING TICKETS AVAILABLE Honky Tonk Holiday Show! Bill Kirchen and his Turtle Doves will make a stop on their annual Honky Tonk Holiday Tour at The Grey Eagle on Mon 12/8. Featured is a sleigh-full of rarely heard holiday numbers from the blues, rock ‚Äòn' roll and honky tonk bags: "Silent Surfin' Night," "Truckin' Trees for Christmas," "Santa Claus Wants Some Lovin," and more. But be ye not afraid, there'll be so much more than holiday songs of questionable taste; you can count on a truckload of dieselbilly classics, rockers, and country weepers to take the edge off the holiday fuss. So mark your calendars and check 'em twice - Santa Claus is back in town! BILL KIRCHEN Bill Kirchen is one of the fortunate few who can step on any stage, play those trademark guitar licks which he created for the seminal Commander Cody classic, "Hot Rod Lincoln," and elicit immediate recognition. As a founding father of the proto-Americana group Commander Cody and his Lost Planet Airmen, Kirchen wrought a diesel-fueled guitar hook that drove their Hot Rod Lincoln into the Top 10 nationwide. Kirchen went on to the Grammys where he was nominated for Best Country Instrumental in 2001. He has recorded with Elvis Costello, Nick Lowe, Dan Hicks, Maria Muldaur, Hoyt Axton, Hazel Dickens, Gene Vincent and Link Wray, and has toured the world as guitarist with Cody, Nick Lowe, Hoyt Axton and Emmylou Harris. Bill Kirchen was inducted into the Hall Of Fame of the Washington DC Wammie Music Awards in 2001, alongside Dave Grohl and John Phillip Sousa. He joined a remarkable list of prior inductees including Bo Diddly, Duke Ellington, Ruth Brown, Marvin Gaye, Patsy Cline, Shirley Horn, Emmylou Harris, Jorma Kaukonen and Jack Casady. His recent disc, Transatlanticana, entered the Americana Radio Chart Top 10 in 2018, joining his extensive catalogue of over 2 dozen albums, from the Commander Cody discs on through his current 12 releases on the Proper and Last Music Company labels. Bill's latest releases are Back from the Ozone, a Lost Planet Airmen reunion CD out in October 2023 and, from 2021, the LPs Waxworks and Tombstone Every Mile, along with The Proper Years and Tombstone on CD and in all digital formats, all on the Last Music Company label. Washington Post: "Seldom has traveling across the rock and country landscape been this much fun" Guitar Player Magazine: "The Titan of the Telecaster‚Ä¶cuts loose with some of the fattest, gnarliest low-down twang imaginable"

In-Person Connection Practice: Art 
When: Mon, Dec 8, 6:30 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: SeekHealing Asheville
Tags: Art, Wellness, Spiritual
Description: You will be provided with your sanitized supplies, or feel free to bring your own colored pencils, markers, or other art supplies to express yourself during this Connection Practice Meeting.

A Connection Practice is a meeting to practice your skills in listening and connecting with others. No conversation topic is off limits. The only objective of the meeting is to feel a genuine sense of connection by the time it's over, and the only rule is that we promise to not give each other advice.

One seeker always facilitates the meeting (to guide the conversation, manage time, and introduce different exercises to help the group feel connected), and another always volunteers as Space Owl (to step aside with anyone who has a big emotional experience and needs 1-on-1 connection).

There is no hierarchy in Connection Practice meetings, and everyone is encouraged to share equally and freely, including the person who facilitates. All connection practices are free of charge.

Trolls: A Field Study
When: Tue, Dec 9, 8:00 AM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: The North Carolina Arboretum
Tags: Art, Outdoors, Family
Description: Something extraordinary is coming to Asheville this winter! The North Carolina Arboretum and Explore Asheville are elated to announce the arrival of Trolls: A Field Study. Visiting on their first North American excursion, these twelve interactive troll sculptures will explore the Arboretum, embarking on a curious journey to learn about humankind. 

Produced by Imagine in collaboration with Danish artist Thomas Dambo, these friendly and fanciful sculptures evoke a sense of wonder and intrigue as they study our small, intricate and inventive ways of life in Western North Carolina. Standing seven to nine feet tall and lovingly described by the artist as ‚ÄúBaby Trolls‚Äù, the creatures are crafted from materials like fallen branches, wooden pallets and twigs. 

Through their observations, the trolls reveal a fresh perspective on what makes us human, sparking curiosity and laughter in visitors of all ages. 

Admission to Trolls: A Field Study is included in the standard Arboretum parking fee. Advance tickets are not required.

When: Tue, Dec 9, 9:00 AM
Where: Asheville, NC

Host: Wortham Center for the Performing Arts
Tags: Fitness, Wellness, Spiritual
Description: **Tuesdays, 9:00‚Äì10:00 am**

September 2, 9, 23, 30 / October 7, 14, 21, 28 / November 4, 11, 18, 25 / December 2, 9, 16, 23

**Henry LaBrun Studio at the Wortham Center** | **Instructor: Miranda Watson**

This class connects the breath with movement to calm and soothe the nervous system and soften the body, mind, and spirit into openness and stillness. Miranda encourages mindfulness and present moment awareness as she skillfully guides students through a slow and fluid sequence of seated, standing, and reclined postures that encourage improved flexibility, range of motion, balance, coordination, and strength. Modifications are offered to dial up or dial down a pose to aid each student in finding the just right level of sensation in the body. Scenic AVL #3:  Kennilworth
When: Tue, Dec 9, 5:45 PM
Where: Asheville, NC
Price: Free
Host: The Asheville Hiking Group
Tags: Outdoors, Fitness, Tours
Description: This route includes the Kenilworth neighborhood and the historically diverse South Asheville neighborhood. We will stop at a historic church and cemetery, as well as Kenilworth Park and Chiles House. We will go up Reservoir Rd to take in the view and get a workout.

**Rating: Moderate**
**Distance:** 5 miles
**Pace:** 3.2 mph
**Elevation:** 670 feet
**Surface:** Road
**Type:** Butterfly Loop
**Gear:** 2L water, snack, poles for the climb
**Features:** Neighborhood charm Kenilworth, a little history, and views from the top. Not likely to see bears.
**Dogs:** On leash.
**Cautions:** Maintain normal traffic awareness.
**Route:** [Kenilworth to Reservoir Rd ](https://www.alltrails.com/explore/map/kenilworth-to-reservoir-road-overlook-d9e74f4?p=-1&sh=ifwm3x).

Running late - go to the Chil's house [https://maps.app.goo.gl/yreuhyktmjmamPT77](https://maps.app.goo.gl/yreuhyktmjmamPT77)

**Scenic Asheville Series:** There are 9 [hikes](https://docs.google.com/document/d/11ewlUM9OV8I4npc1cNNsSYOnXI0QPw2isAleXdFzEbI/edit?usp=drivesdk) in the series; hike them all and receive an [attractive badge](https://docs.google.com/drawings/d/1goXUXfzUBqhB4_UeCxodlk4ZPeCCgqZrWK2EUJvk_vI/edit) for your backpack.
Badge Holders are always welcome on all hikes, even if you are on the waitlist.

**On-Time Departure**
I typically have 1 or 2 no-shows on my hikes, so we don't wait for people to arrive. If you are late, you'll be left behind

* If you no-show 2 times without changing your RSVP and/or contacting the hike leader, you may be blocked from the group.
* Please note that there is never cell coverage at the start of the hike, so please change your RSVP as soon as you know you can't make it.
* Notes and comments are genuinely appreciated.

**Guests:** Please ask guests to sign up for the hike themselves.

**Disclaimer and Release of Liability:**
This activity involves hiking on city streets that may have traffic. Participants are responsible for their safety on streets and trails. The organizer of this trip is a volunteer and not a professional guide. The function of the organizer is only to organize this trip. If you sign up or participate in this event you acknowledge that you freely and voluntarily agree to assume all risks of injuries, illnesses, and damages arising from, as a result of, and associated with this event. In addition, you acknowledge that you agree to the Meetup terms: https://www.meetup.com/terms
